<a id="t-494aa01955"></a>
## Thread: Zero client web development — 4 msgs

_Topics: [`Web, XML, modern integration`](topics.md#web)_

### Zero client web development

- **From:** Mattc <mpcsoft6@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-08-30T05:46:35-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<1fa05dcb-eb47-4f67-895a-41e88021090e@a7g2000yqb.googlegroups.com>`

```
I am soliciting opinions.  I run a payroll service using my own
(developed in COBOL) payroll system, but I'd like to put on the web 2
or 3 small zero client web services: a time clock to record
attendance, a free payroll calculator and a free loan calculator.
Using the platform I have, I can implement these tools on the web, but
the particular software that allows this is clunky and involves 2-3
layers of things that do not necessarily play well together.  I could
re-develop these relatively simply tools in C# or VB or Java or even
Python, but would ultimately need to import the data they produce back
into my COBOL payroll system.

My question is this: if any of you were doing this, job, which
development environment would you choose?  These services will reside
on a WIndows server.  Thanks in advance for any opinions you might put
forth.  I read this newsgroup every day; have been a COBOL programmer
since 1974 and enjoy your conversations immensely!  Thanks again.  --
Mattc
```

#### ↳ Re: Zero client web development

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-08-31T01:55:45+12:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9c48f1FitbU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<1fa05dcb-eb47-4f67-895a-41e88021090e@a7g2000yqb.googlegroups.com>`

```
Mattc wrote:
> I am soliciting opinions.  I run a payroll service using my own
> (developed in COBOL) payroll system, but I'd like to put on the web 2
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> Mattc

Matt,

this looks like it might be an Oracle-RTD application?

If it is, you can generate the Web Services in Java and set a listener to 
cause a callback on your COBOL code. (In effect, it is like raising an 
interrupt when data is posted by the service.)

If I am way off the beam and this is not your environment let me start 
again... :-)

What you are REALLY asking is: How can I collect data from a Web Service and 
give it to my COBOL application (which is not necessarily running on the web 
server - however it must be ACCESSIBLE from the web server)?

There are 2 possibilities, and the programming language really doesn't 
matter... you should use whatever you are most comfortable with and can do 
the job. If it were me, I'd use C# because (a) I already have a fair bit of 
experience at calling COBOL from C# and vice versa and (b) I enjoy doing 
tricky things in C#... YMMV.

1. You can use a mailbox approach with the web services posting data and the 
COBOL app. periodically checking the "mailbox". It doesn't have to be a real 
mailbox; could be a table on a shared DB, or even a file on the server. 
(This is kind of like "polling" and is for wimps and girls...)

2. You can trigger an event directly from the web service. (This is kind of 
like "interrupt driven" and is what real men do...)

I would take approach 2 every time.

However you need a proxy for your COBOL app. and you need some remoting and 
...Hang on a minute!

Proxy? Remote Procedure calls?

This is a job for.... ta! da!   http://www.xml-rpc.net/

...  or somethng like it... :-)

Pete.
```

#### ↳ Re: Zero client web development

- **From:** Richard <riplin@Azonic.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-08-30T11:50:15-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6abd06dc-5476-4a51-8d35-2238f9778f87@x21g2000prd.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<1fa05dcb-eb47-4f67-895a-41e88021090e@a7g2000yqb.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Aug 31, 12:46 am, Mattc <mpcso...@gmail.com> wrote:
> I am soliciting opinions.  I run a payroll service using my own
> (developed in COBOL) payroll system, but I'd like to put on the web 2
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> Mattc

It is not difficult to do CGI in COBOL. I developed some systems using
this back in the 90s and some still run. It even does AJAX (which is
just another interaction on the server side).

Most of my stuff these days is in Python on the server side.

You will probably need to use Javascript on the client side. I use
jQuery which makes it easy to do browser based UIs without worrying
about which browser is being used.

The major issue is that you should be using templates to generate the
web pages. This makes it simple to change and tune the pages without
(usually) having to change the server code.

CGI, templating and other web based stuff is not difficult in COBOL
and does give the ability to interact directly with the existing
system including record locking.

I posted some of my COBOL code on Google groups:

See if this works of search for CGIINPUT.CBL

http://groups.google.com/group/comp.lang.cobol/tree/browse_frm/thread/279ec8d61bd1fdfa/589c20d9e16f26b2?rnum=1&q=cgidata&_done=%2Fgroup%2Fcomp.lang.cobol%2Fbrowse_frm%2Fthread%2F279ec8d61bd1fdfa%2F0efba58bcc1ab315%3Flnk%3Dgst%26q%3Dcgidata%26
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Zero client web development

- **From:** Mattc <mpcsoft6@gmail.com>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<d2a31cd8-37f0-4c34-a03f-dccbabb777da@dp9g2000vbb.googlegroups.com>`


###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Using OpenCobol to convert a fixed size EBCDIC file to ASCII?

_(thread depth: 4)_

- **From:** Louis Krupp <lkrupp@nospam.indra.com.invalid>
- **Date:** 2011-08-31T05:57:26-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b47s57dafe4qau7aedalljo6rdr2oggs4t@4ax.com>`
- **References:** `<7cd33e25-b4a7-4724-8da4-3dfa765ed793@ea4g2000vbb.googlegroups.com> <mgfq57h0rmla3s5jvbj2jak901r19adt9c@4ax.com> <j3jhvu$qpf$1@dont-email.me> <d731d61a-edc6-40d3-b76b-d1a129646fd5@z7g2000vbp.googlegroups.com>`

```
On Tue, 30 Aug 2011 23:20:36 -0700 (PDT), Vincent <hrchl86@gmail.com>
wrote:

>On Aug 30, 4:42ï¿½pm, Kerry Liles
><"kerry.liles[minus_the_spam]"@gmail.com> wrote:
…[38 more quoted lines elided]…
>Indeed, it is so complicated since the fields are packed..

Are all of the fields packed, or just some of them?

If all of the fields are packed, then you don't have to do any EBCDIC
to ASCII conversion.

If some of the fields are packed, then as Kerry pointed out, it gets
complicated.

I would consider writing a C function -- call it e2a -- to convert n
bytes at address p from EBCDIC to ASCII.  You might be able to use one
of the tables here:

http://www.opensource.apple.com/source/OpenSSL/OpenSSL-16/openssl/crypto/ebcdic.c

Your COBOL program could do something like this:

1.  READ the input file
2.  CALL "e2a" using field1 LENGTH OF field1
     CALL "e2a" using field2 LENGTH OF field2
     etc for each DISPLAY field that must be converted
3.  WRITE the record to the output file
4.  READ the input file again

Coding this would be tedious, but you might be able to write a script
or a program that would read a list of field names and generate the
CALL statements.

Have fun.

Louis
```

## Thread: OT: Cobol jokes — 3 this month / 43 total

_Topics: [`Off-topic and spam`](topics.md#spam)_

### OT: Cobol jokes

- **From:** Alistair Maclean <alistair.j.l.maclean@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-08-30T07:01:01-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<8f0964ad-b00b-425f-b759-24db3d54b360@s20g2000yql.googlegroups.com>`

```
When responding to Vinces query I came across these:

•What did COBOL yell to the escaping thief?

STOP RUN RETURNING NOW.


•A COBOL programmer's husband asks, "Honey can you go to the store and
get some milk. And if they have eggs, get a dozen." After twenty
minutes she returns and flops 12 bags of milk on the table. He looks
at her curiously, "Honey, why did you do that?" She responds flatly,
"They had eggs."



•What did COBOL reply to the executive? Yes, I can

PERFORM JUMPS THRU HOOPS.

or

PERFORM JUMPS THRU FLAMING-HOOPS UNTIL HELL-FREEZES-OVER.
```
